Jamison Brereton

1 (442)
Agni
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
13 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
A rather stately hymn, appropriate for the first in the Agni sequence in Maс╣Зс╕Нala VI. It concerns only the ritual fire, with almost no mention of its physical substance, and unlike the typical dawn kindling sequence, the hymn depicts the arrival and installation of Agni as Hotar and, especially, the ritual fire as joint possession and responsibility of the whole ─Аrya community, as Proferes (2007: 33) points out. As the first hymn in the maс╣Зс╕Нala, it thus establishes an image of a settled and well-ordered society unified in its devotion to the gods to which the rest of the maс╣Зс╕Нala will be dedicated.
The arrival and installation occupy verses 1тАУ3; verses 4тАУ8 show AgniтАЩs reach through the community, from the individual house, to the clan and settlements, and indeed to all who claim Manu (the first sacrificer) as ancestor. Verses 9тАУ10 detail the homage and service Agni deserves, and the remaining verses (11тАУ13) the favors we ask in return.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou Agni, are the first of the gods; a deity to whom their minds are devoted; plural asing of aspect, you are the invoker of the deities at this rite; showerer (of benefits), bestow upon us unsurpassable strength, where with to sustain all (hostile) prowess.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tvam hi agne prathamo manot─Б: manot─Б is interpreted as dev─Бn ─Бm mano yatrotam, sambaddham, where, on whom, the mind of the gods is attached; or, dev─Бn─Бm man─Бс╣Гsi et─Бni dс╣Ыс╕Нhapraviс╣гс╣н─Бni yasy─Бm devat─Бy─Бm sa manot─Б, the divinity on whom the minds of the gods are fastened, that is, firmly concentrated, he is called manot─Б: Agniс╕е sarv─Б manot─Бgnau manot─Бс╕е saс╣Гgacchante (Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 2.10)

Jamison Brereton

You, o Agni, as first minder of this insightful thought here, became the Hotar, o wondrous one.
You, o bull, made (the thought) into power difficult to surpass, to
overpower all (other) power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted ad loc., the first hymn of Maс╣Зс╕Нala IV begins identically (IV.1.1.a): tv├бс╣Г h├н agne, with the same puzzling use of ordinarily causal h├н in the first p─Бda of a hymn. It might be possible here to tr. the first hemistich as a causal clause subordinate to cd: тАЬBecause тАж you became the first minder of this insightful thought and the Hotar, you made тАжтАЭ On the stem man├│tar- see comm. ad II.9.4 and IV.1.16, 5.10. Note also that the Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition pausal resolution of the word as man├│ta is faulty; it should end in a long -─Б.

Geldner construes the gen. asy─Б╠Бdhiy├бс╕е with both man├│t─Б and h├│t─Б, but the latter doesnтАЩt usually govern a genitive.

The s─лm in c presumably refers to the dh─л╠Б- of b. The published translation could be slightly altered to тАЬmade it into power тАжтАЭ; so Geldner тАЬтАж machtest es zu тАж Macht.тАЭ On the infinitival construction in cd, see also Keydana (253). Note the attraction of the object of s├бhadhyai into the dative case (v├н┼Ыvasmai s├бhase). P─Бda d is also noteworthy in having three forms of тИЪsah, though two belong to the same s-stem.

Griffith

THOU, first inventor of this prayer, O Agni, Worker of Marvels, hast become our Herald.
Thou, Bull, hast made us strength which none may conquer, strength that shall overcome all other prowess.

рдЕрдз рдЕрдзреБрдирд╛ рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдпрдЬреАрдпрд╛рдиреН рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реЛрдордирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдХрдГ рд╕рдиреН рдЗрд│рдГ рднреВрдореНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдкрджреЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдиреНрдпрд╕реАрджрдГ рдирд┐рд╖рдгреНрдгрд╡рд╛рдирд╕рд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН ред рдЗрд╖рдпрдиреН рдкрд╢реБрдкреБрд░реЛрдбрд╛рд╢рд╛рджрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдордиреНрдирдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдИрдбреНрдпрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрдГ рд╕рдиреН ред рддрдВ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдердордореН рдЗрддрд░рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рднреНрдпрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдВ рджреЗрд╡рдпрдиреНрддрдГ рджреЗрд╡рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдорд╛рддреНрдорди рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ рдирд░рдГ рдиреЗрддрд╛рд░реЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЧреНрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдорд╣рдГ рдорд╣рддреЗ рд░рд╛рдпреЗ рдзрдирд╛рдп рдЪрд┐рддрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдпрдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдиреБ рдЧреНрдордиреН рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOfferer of the oblation, frequent celebrator of sacrifice, now sit down on the foot-m ark of Iс╕╖─Б, accepting the (sacrirficial) food, and being glorified; devout men, expectant of great riches, have recourse to you as to the first (of the gods).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Then you sat down as Hotar, superior sacrificer, prospering in the footprint of refreshment, to be reverently invoked.
You are the first that men have followed when they seek the gods,
distinguishing themselves greatly for wealth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b ends with one of the rare examples of non-concessive s├бn, nom. sg. m.

pres. part. to тИЪas. Its presence here may be due to an effort at metrical adjustment.

The stem ─лс╕Нi ya- is almost invariably read distracted as here, and it is extremely common in p─Бda-final position. This is fine for dimeter meter and for Jagat─л, but the distracted stem obviously doesnтАЩt fit a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence. The addition of monosyllabic s├бn allows such a cadence here. Note also that s├бn rhymes with gman, which closes the next two hemistichs (2d, 3b). The only ex. of a non-distracted form of ─л╠Бс╕Нya- (save for a lone Xth Maс╣Зс╕Нala gen. sg.) is found likewise in a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence in IV.24.2 s├б vс╣Ыtrah├бtye h├бvyaс╕е s├б ─л╠Бс╕Нyaс╕е, where a non-distracted ─л╠Бс╕Нyaс╕е sits uncomfortably after a distracted h├бvi yaс╕е. So, two different solutions to the problem of fitting ─л╠Бс╕Нya- into a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence.

Geldner suggests that the second hemistich тАЬspielt auf AgniтАЩs Flucht ins Wasser an.тАЭ I donтАЩt myself see this, and I do not know what his evidence is, beyond ├бnu gman тАШhave followedтАЩ. In this ritual context, the тАЬgod-seeking menтАЭ тАЬhave followed Agni first,тАЭ because he is the conduit of their offerings to the gods and the divinity who is installed in their own houses. They must go through him, as it were, to reach the gods.

The first hemistich emphasizes this ritual connection: Agni тАЬsits downтАЭ (that is, is installed) as Hotar and superior sacrificer, and the place where he is installed is specified as тАЬthe footprint of refreshmentтАЭ (iс╕╖├бs pad├й), a kenning for the ritual ground (see, for a similar installation scenario, I.128.1 and II.10.1).

On mah├│ r─Бy├й see comm. ad IV.31.11. The interp. of the rest of p─Бda d is uncertain, primarily because of the multiply ambiguous cit├бya- stem. The p─Бda most resembles V.15.5 mah├│ r─Бy├й cit├бyann ├бtrim aspah, rendered by Geldner as тАЬdu hast jetzt zu grossem Reichtum dich offenbarend dem Atri (aus der Not) herausgeholfenтАЭ (though in our passage here he takes cit├бyantaс╕е as тАЬaufmerksam,тАЭ a completely different sense of cit├бya-) and in the published translation (JPB) as тАЬтАжthen appearing greatly for wealth, you have rescued Atri.тАЭ My published translation here (тАЬdistinguishing themselvesтАЭ) is closest to GeldnerтАЩs tr. of V.15.5, though I think it adds a crucial element. The point must (or at least may) be that the men seek to make especially conspicuous offerings to the gods, via Agni, for the sake of acquiring the wealth that accrues to the successful sacrificer. The apparent reflexive tr. тАШdistinguish oneselfтАЩ is really just an extension of the common value of cit├бya- тАШappearтАЩ/ тАШappear (good), be conspicuousтАЩ. RenouтАЩs тАЬfixant leur pens├йe sur la richesse (pour l’atteindre) grandementтАЭ is an extension of GeldnerтАЩs тАЬattentiveтАЭ sense, but I think he has extended too far.

Griffith

As Priest thou sattest at the seat of worship, furthering us, best Offerer, meet for honour.
So first to thee have pious men resorted, turning thy mind to thoughts of ample riches.

Geldner

Darum setztest du, der opfert├╝chtige Hotri dich nieder an der St├дtte der Labung, Labung genie├Яend als der zu Berufende. Als solchem gingen dir zuerst die gottergebenen M├дnner nach, aufmerksam, um den gro├Яen Schatz zu gewinnen.

Grassmann

Dann setztest du am Andachtsort dich nieder, als bester Opfrer, preisenswerth, erlabend; Drum strebten dir die gottergebnen M├дnner als erstem nach auf grosse Habe sinnend.

Elizarenkova

рд╡реГрддреЗрд╡ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗрдг ред рдЗрд╡реЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ ред рд▓реЛрдХрджреНрд╡рдпрдордзреНрдпрдЧрддреЗрди рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗрдг рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рдГ рдЕрдиреЗрдХреИрдГ рд╡рд╕рд╡реНрдпреИрдГ рд╡рд╕реБрднрд┐рдГ рее рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдХрд╕реНрддрджреНрдзрд┐рддрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпреИрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╛рд░реНрдзрдВ рдпрдиреНрддрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН рдЕрдиреБ рдЧреНрдордиреН рдЕрдиреБрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕рдВрднрдЬрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреЗ ред рддреНрд╡реЗ рддреНрд╡рдпрд┐ рджреЗрд╡реЗ рд░рдпрд┐рдВ рдзрдирдВ рдЬрд╛рдЧреГрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд░реБрд╢рдиреНрддрдВ рджреАрдкреНрддрд╡рд░реНрдгрдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрдирд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рджрд░реНрд╢рддрдВ рджрд░реНрд╢рдиреАрдпрдВ рдмреГрд╣рдиреНрддрдВ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рд╡рдкрд╛рд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╣рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрд╖реБ рджреАрджрд┐рд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдВ рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThose who are assiduous in (worshipping) you for riches follow you, going with many Vasus by the path (of the firmament); you, the radiant Agni, of goodly aspect, mighty, fed with burnt-offerings, and blazing every day.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The wakeful ones have followed (you) when you come with many goods as if with a troop, (and they follow) the wealth nearby youтАФ
gleaming Agni, lovely to see, lofty, who receives the omentum (of the sacrificial beast as offering), shining through all the days.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich of this vs. presents some difficulties. One of the problems is that the acc. y├бntam in the first p─Бda most naturally invites Agni as referent, since the main verb of the clause, ├бnu gman, is the same as in 2cd, where Agni was definitely the acc. complement. But in p─Бda b Agni is represented by a loc. tv├й and there is a different acc. ray├нm. One solution has been to construe ray├нm loosely (or not so loosely) with the pf. part. j─Бgс╣Ыv─Б╠Бс╣Гsaс╕е, leaving y├бntam in p─Бda a as the only acc. with ├бnu gman. This is the solution Oldenberg favors (ZDMG 55.271-72 = KlSch 730- 31: тАЬbei dir Reichtum erwachendтАЭ), but тИЪgс╣Ы тАШbe awakeтАЩ does not otherwise take an acc. Both Geldner and Renou supply a parenthetical non-finite verb more or less dependent on j─Бgс╣Ыv─Б╠Бс╣Гsaс╕е to govern тАШwealthтАЩ: тАЬdas sie bei dir Reichtum (erwartend) gewacht habenтАЭ and тАЬтАж vigilants, (pour atteindre) en toi la richesse.тАЭ Since I prefer not to supply anything I donтАЩt have to, IтАЩve tried another tack – making y├бntam (with Agni as referent) and ray├нm conjoined goals of ├бnu gman. In other words, the wakeful men (presumably the priests alert at the sacrifice) pursue both Agni as he comes with goods and the goods themselves that are nearby him after he has deposited them on the ritual ground. I donтАЩt, however, find this very satisfactory – though I donтАЩt find the other possibilities satisfying either (and I simply donтАЩt understand LudwigтАЩs interpr., as reported by Oldenberg, 271-72 = 730-31). Somewhat in favor of my interpr. is RenouтАЩs comment that tv├й ray├нm тАж ├бnu gman is a тАЬvariation inorganiqueтАЭ (whatever he means by that adj.) of tv─Б .. r─Бy├й тАж ├бnu gman. I would rephrase it slightly to say that my тАЬthey follow you and wealthтАЭ(3ab) is a variant (inorganic or not) of тАЬthey follow you for wealthтАЭ (2cd).

In any case, the string of accusatives in cd all clearly refer to Agni, and we are back on firm ground.

Griffith

In thee, still watching, they have followed riches, who goest with much wealth as with an army,
The radiant Agni, lofty, fair to look on, worshipped with marrow, evermore resplendent.

Ihm, der mit vielen Sch├дtzen wie ein H├дuptling mit seinem Gefolge auszog, sind sie nachgegangen, da sie bei dir Reichtum erwartend gewacht haben, dem hellen Agni, dem gerngesehenen, hohen, der mit einer Netzhaut versehen allezeit leuchtet.

Die, welche Gaben brachten, flehn den Gott an, der wie umschart von vielen G├╝tern herkommt, Den lichten, grossen, sehenswerthen Agni, den fettumh├╝llten, welcher stetig leuchtet.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMen desirous of food obtain abundance unopposed when repairing to the station of the divinity with oblations; and when delighting, Agni, in your auspicious presence, they repeat those your names which are to be uttered at sacrifices.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

They repeat those your names: n─Бm─Бni cid dadhire yaj├▒─лy─Бni, that is, such appellations as j─Бtavedas, vai┼Ыv─Бnara, and means of adoration, stotr─Бс╣Зi namanas─Бdhan─Бni

Jamison Brereton

Pursuing the track of the god with homage, seeking fame, they will attain fame indestructible;
even the names they have assumed are worthy of worship. They take pleasure in your auspicious manifestation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again Geldner claims that this verse is about the myth of the flight of Agni, presumably on the basis of pad├бm dev├бsya тАж vy├бntaс╕е, but the track of the god doesn’t have to be his flight, but simply the ritual cursus.

How one interprets the larger sense of the vs. depends on how one interprets the verb forms: ─Бpan, dadhire, and raс╣Зayanta, esp. the first. Both Geldner and Renou take ─Бpan as preterital (тАЬтАж haben sie тАж erlangt,тАЭ тАЬont obtenuтАЭ), presumably taking it as a pluperfect or a thematic aorist (both either augmented or not) to тИЪ─Бp, and Geldner clearly thinks the subj. is the Aс╣Еgirases. (Grassmann takes it as an aor.) But nothing prevents it from being a pf. subjunctive. In that case, the priests pursuing the ritual cursus in a, who are seeking fame (┼Ыravasy├бvaс╕е), will obtain fame through their priestly activities. The pf. dadhire in c can then have, as often, immediate past reference (тАЬthey have assumed namesтАЭ - presumably their priestly titles), and the injunctive raс╣Зayanta in d is easily compatible with that scenario as a general timeless presential. Because of the otherwise exclusive focus on the ritual function of Agni in this hymn, my interpr.

seems preferable to one that goes haring off into the mythological past.

Note ┼Ыr├бvaс╕е тАж ├бmс╣Ыktam тАЬindestructible fameтАЭ as a variation on the formula ┼Ыr├бvaс╕е тАж ├бkс╣гitam.

Griffith

They who approached the God’s abode with homage, eager for glory, won them perfect glory:
Yea, they gained even sacrificial titles, and found delight in thine auspicious aspect.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMen exalt you upon earth; they exalt you for both kinds of affluence, (cattle and treasure, which you bestow upon) men; you who extricate (us from evil) are to be known as our preserver, as the unfailing father and mother of mankind.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Which you bestow upon, men: jan─Бn─Бm may also mean, for the gift of men, that is, of male posterity

Jamison Brereton

You do the settlements strengthen on earth; you (do) both of the тАЬriches of the peoplesтАЭ [=patrons and singers?] (strengthen).
You, o surpassing oneтАФbecome a rescuer worthy of note, a father, a mother forever for the sons of Manu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The referent of the phrase тАЬboth riches of the peopleтАЭ (r─Б╠Бya ubh├бy─Бso j├бn─Бn─Бm) is not entirely clear. The standard assumption is that it refers to material goods of some sort, but which are the two kinds? Geldner (n. 5b) cites S─Бyaс╣Зa on the TB for heavenly and earthly riches – though S─Бyaс╣Зa on our passage suggests rather (domestic) animals and non-animals (pa┼Ыvapa┼Ыur┼лp─Бс╣Зi). GeldnerтАЩs own suggestion is our own goods and those of our enemies, based on VII.83.5 yuv├бс╣Г h├н v├бsva ubh├бyasya r─Б╠Бjathaс╕е, where the published translation (jpb) tentatively suggests rather those of war and peace. Acdg. to Renou, they are material and spiritual goods, which he thinks are ray├н- and v├бsurespectively – a completely arbitrary and ad hoc differentiation of these two extremely common stems, not supported in other passages as far as I can see. GeldnerтАЩs interpr. is more plausible, but it seems strange to announce that goods of whatever sort тАЬstrengthenтАЭ Agni – esp. as in vss. 2-3 Agni is depicted as the bringer and provider of goods for us. I have a completely different view of the phrase – that it refers metaphorically to manpower. In VI.14.3 the тАЬriches of the strangerтАЭ (r─Б╠Бyo ary├бс╕е) contend with each other (sp├бrdhante), where the verb invites an animate referent for the subject. Moreover, ubh├бya- regularly refers to two different groups of beings: e.g., I.60.2 ubh├бy─Бsaс╕е тАж u┼Ы├нjo y├й ca m├бrt─Бс╕е тАЬboth тАж his (ancient) priests and mortals (now)тАЭ; II.2.12 ubh├бy─Бsaс╕е тАж stot─Б╠Бraс╕е тАж s┼лr├бya┼Ы ca тАЬboth praisers and patrons.тАЭ In II.6.7 j├бnmobh├бy─Б тАЬboth breedsтАЭ refers to the human and divine races, similarly j─Бt─Б╠Бm╠Рubh├бy─Бn in IV.2.2. Here either human/divine or patrons/singers (or some other division of mortals) would be possible, but I favor the latter, given the concentration on humans and their ritual activities here.

рд╕рдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╕рдкрд░реНрдпреЗрдгреНрдпрдГ рдкреВрдЬреНрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреВрд░рдХрдГ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реБ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реЛрдордирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдХрдГ рдордиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдорджрдиреАрдпрдГ рдпрдЬреАрдпрд╛рдиреН рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдЗрддрд░рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдпрдЬрдирд╛рдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреБрднрд╛рд╡реЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдирд┐ рд╖рд╕рд╛рдж рдирд┐рд╖рдгреНрдгреЛрд╜рднреВрддреН ред рдЕрде рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдХреГрддрдГред рддрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╡рдпрдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рджрдореЗ рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рджреАрджрд┐рд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдВ рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЬреНрдЮреБрдмрд╛рдзрдГ рдЬрд╛рдиреБрдиреА рдмрд╛рдзрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рдЕрд╡рдирддрдЬрд╛рдирд╡рдГ рдкреНрд░рдгрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рдирдорд╕рд╛ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗрдг рдЙрдк рдЖ рд╕рджреЗрдо рдЖрд╕рд╛рджрдпреЗрдо ред рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕реАрджреЗрдореЗрддреНрдпреЗрд╡рдорд╛рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреЗ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, who is adorable, affectionate, the offerer of oblations among men, the giver of delight, the celebrator of worship, has sat down (upon the altar); let us approach you, kindled in our dwellings, on bended knees, with praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Dear Agni is to be served among the clans. As Hotar he has sat down, the gladdening superior sacrificer.
You, shining in our house, do we reverently approach, on bended knee, with homage.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b h├│t─Б тАж n├н с╣гas─Бda y├бj─лy─Бn closely echoes 2a ├бdh─Б h├│t─Б ny ├аs─лdo y├бj─лy─Бn. The opening of p─Бda c (as well as 7a), t├бс╣Г tv─Б, also matches 2c, and d─лdiv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam of c matches the same adj. in 3d.

Whatever the exact posture described by j├▒ub─Б╠Бdhaс╕е (for detailed disc. see Scarlatta 343-45), the Engl. idiom тАЬon bended kneeтАЭ conveys the same sense of physical reverence.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand why 6c has the act. pf. part. d─лdiv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam while, in the same metrical position, qualifying the same entity, and apparently meaning the same thing, 7c has the middle part. d─л╠Бdiy─Бnaс╕е (whose tense-aspect stem affiliation is not entirely clear: its accent weakly suggests that it already belongs to the new redupl.

pres. [reinterpreted from the pf.], but the redupl. forms to this root are in flux; see my тАЬperfect impvтАЭ paper in the Lubotsky Fs.). Of course a nom. form of the act. part would not fit this slot in 7c, but an acc. form of the middle part. would be fine in 6c. I doubt that the poet is contrasting old perfect and new pres., or trying to draw a semantic difference between the voices. The participle d─л╠Бdiy─Бna- is the only medial form to this root; all the finite forms are active, with intrans. value, as are the two act.

participles, old-style pf. d─лdiv─Б╠Бс╣Гs- and new-style redupl. pres. d─л╠Бdyant-.

VI.1.7-8: Both Geldner and Renou take n├бvyam in 7a as an adv. (e.g., тАЬaufs neueтАЭ), but since the adj. n├бvya- in the nom. (hence not a possible adverb) regularly qualifies Agni (V.12.3, VII.4.8, VIII.11.10, X.4.5), I see no reason not to take it as an adj. here. The reference of course is to the newly kindled ritual fire.

Geldner, flg. Ludwig, thinks that 7c concerns battle, which again I find difficult to see. I am more persuaded by ProferesтАЩs reading (pp. 29-30), that the hymn in general presents Agni as the fire held in common by the larger community and that in vss. 7- 8 тАЬthis common fire is a symbol of centralized sovereignty,тАЭ therefore a leader of the clans and, in 8a the clan-lord of each and every clan.

Vs. 8 is couched entirely in the acc., referring to Agni. It canтАЩt be directly attached to either what immediately precedes or what immediately follows, since both 7cd and 9ab have Agni in the nom. However, it follows nicely after the accusatives in 7ab, with 7cd an intrusion. To indicate that the description of Agni is in the acc., I have resupplied тАЬwe imploreтАЭ from 7b.

On the semantics of the root тИЪtu┼Ы in nit├│┼Ыana-, see comm. ad VIII.38.2.

The hapax cmpd. pr├йt─лс╣гaс╣Зi- is curiously formed and its sense not entirely clear, esp. because the root affiliation of -iс╣гaс╣Зi- is uncertain and because the cmpd type is muddled, at least by its interpreters. Geldner takes the 2nd member with тИЪiс╣г тАШseek, desireтАЩ: тАЬder das Auftreten (des Opferpriesters) w├╝nschtтАЭ; while Renou opts for тИЪiс╣г тАШimpelтАЩ: тАЬqui pousse en avant l’incitation,тАЭ with alternatives in the notes тАЬqui aspire ├а aller de lтАЩavantтАЭ (тИЪiс╣г тАШseek, desireтАЩ) or тАЬqui fait avancer l’incitation (des humains)тАЭ (тИЪiс╣г тАШimpelтАЩ). The тАШseek, desireтАЩ root is also represented by DebrunnerтАЩs тАЬzum Vormarsch strebendтАЭ (AiG II.2.208). In my interpr. I take OldenbergтАЩs point (Noten ad loc.; he doesnтАЩt discuss in ZDMG 55) that the accent suggests a bahuvr─лhi, and I favor a connection of the 2nd member with тИЪiс╣г тАШimpelтАЩ and esp. the 2ndary verbal stems iс╣гanaya- and iс╣гaс╣Зya-, both тАШimpelтАЩ. A literal rendering would then be something like тАЬhaving the impulsion of the forward progress (of the sacrifice),тАЭ but in English the bahuvr─лhi gloss is too awkward, hence my тАЬimpelling тАжтАЭ The point here is that Agni controls the pace and movement of the sacrifice, which progress is often expressed by the idiom pr├б тИЪi (cf. the common loc. absol. prayaty ├аdhvar├й тАЬwhile the ceremony is advancingтАЭ) found in the 1st member pr├йti-. The 2nd member iс╣гaс╣Зi- is immediately followed by the part. iс╣г├бyantam, but I think this is a playful juxtaposition: the two words have nothing to do with each other, and the sense тАШprosperingтАЩ for the latter was established in the fuller expression in 2b.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand why 6c has the act. pf. part. d─лdiv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam while, in the same metrical position, qualifying the same entity, and apparently meaning the same thing, 7c has the middle part. d─л╠Бdiy─Бnaс╕е (whose tense-aspect stem affiliation is not entirely clear: its accent weakly suggests that it already belongs to the new redupl.

pres. [reinterpreted from the pf.], but the redupl. forms to this root are in flux; see my тАЬperfect impvтАЭ paper in the Lubotsky Fs.). Of course a nom. form of the act. part would not fit this slot in 7c, but an acc. form of the middle part. would be fine in 6c. I doubt that the poet is contrasting old perfect and new pres., or trying to draw a semantic difference between the voices. The participle d─л╠Бdiy─Бna- is the only medial form to this root; all the finite forms are active, with intrans. value, as are the two act.

participles, old-style pf. d─лdiv─Б╠Бс╣Гs- and new-style redupl. pres. d─л╠Бdyant-.

VI.1.7-8: Both Geldner and Renou take n├бvyam in 7a as an adv. (e.g., тАЬaufs neueтАЭ), but since the adj. n├бvya- in the nom. (hence not a possible adverb) regularly qualifies Agni (V.12.3, VII.4.8, VIII.11.10, X.4.5), I see no reason not to take it as an adj. here. The reference of course is to the newly kindled ritual fire.

Geldner, flg. Ludwig, thinks that 7c concerns battle, which again I find difficult to see. I am more persuaded by ProferesтАЩs reading (pp. 29-30), that the hymn in general presents Agni as the fire held in common by the larger community and that in vss. 7- 8 тАЬthis common fire is a symbol of centralized sovereignty,тАЭ therefore a leader of the clans and, in 8a the clan-lord of each and every clan.

Vs. 8 is couched entirely in the acc., referring to Agni. It canтАЩt be directly attached to either what immediately precedes or what immediately follows, since both 7cd and 9ab have Agni in the nom. However, it follows nicely after the accusatives in 7ab, with 7cd an intrusion. To indicate that the description of Agni is in the acc., I have resupplied тАЬwe imploreтАЭ from 7b.

On the semantics of the root тИЪtu┼Ы in nit├│┼Ыana-, see comm. ad VIII.38.2.

The hapax cmpd. pr├йt─лс╣гaс╣Зi- is curiously formed and its sense not entirely clear, esp. because the root affiliation of -iс╣гaс╣Зi- is uncertain and because the cmpd type is muddled, at least by its interpreters. Geldner takes the 2nd member with тИЪiс╣г тАШseek, desireтАЩ: тАЬder das Auftreten (des Opferpriesters) w├╝nschtтАЭ; while Renou opts for тИЪiс╣г тАШimpelтАЩ: тАЬqui pousse en avant l’incitation,тАЭ with alternatives in the notes тАЬqui aspire ├а aller de lтАЩavantтАЭ (тИЪiс╣г тАШseek, desireтАЩ) or тАЬqui fait avancer l’incitation (des humains)тАЭ (тИЪiс╣г тАШimpelтАЩ). The тАШseek, desireтАЩ root is also represented by DebrunnerтАЩs тАЬzum Vormarsch strebendтАЭ (AiG II.2.208). In my interpr. I take OldenbergтАЩs point (Noten ad loc.; he doesnтАЩt discuss in ZDMG 55) that the accent suggests a bahuvr─лhi, and I favor a connection of the 2nd member with тИЪiс╣г тАШimpelтАЩ and esp. the 2ndary verbal stems iс╣гanaya- and iс╣гaс╣Зya-, both тАШimpelтАЩ. A literal rendering would then be something like тАЬhaving the impulsion of the forward progress (of the sacrifice),тАЭ but in English the bahuvr─лhi gloss is too awkward, hence my тАЬimpelling тАжтАЭ The point here is that Agni controls the pace and movement of the sacrifice, which progress is often expressed by the idiom pr├б тИЪi (cf. the common loc. absol. prayaty ├аdhvar├й тАЬwhile the ceremony is advancingтАЭ) found in the 1st member pr├йti-. The 2nd member iс╣гaс╣Зi- is immediately followed by the part. iс╣г├бyantam, but I think this is a playful juxtaposition: the two words have nothing to do with each other, and the sense тАШprosperingтАЩ for the latter was established in the fuller expression in 2b.

Thou, Agni, leddest forth our men to battle, refulgent with the heaven’s exalted splendour.

English translation:

тАЬ(We glorify) the lord of men of ever-existing men; the wise, the destroyer (of foes) the showerer (of benefits) on mankind, the moving, the bestower of food, the purifier, the resplendent, Agni, who is worshipped for (the sake of) riches.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe man, Agni, who worships you, who praises you, who offers oblations to you with kindled fuel, who presents burnt-offerings to you with prostrations, he verily, protected by you, obtains all desired wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Agni, that mortal has sacrificed and ritually labored who after kindling you has achieved your oblation-giving,
who knows his way around the offering with its acts of homage. Just he will acquire all things of value, when aided by you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

There are a few small questions in this vs. In b both Geldner and Renou take instr.

sam├нdh─Б as referring to the concrete material kindling stick, as often – while I think it refers to abstractly to the moment of kindling (as also, in my view, in VI.2.5 and quite possibly VI.5.5). The abstract sense is allowed by Scarlatta (52-53), and the fact that the dat. to the same stem, sam├нdhe, can be used as an infinitive (see, inter alia, Keydana 186 n. 160) supports this interpr. It has to be admitted, though, that the same instr. in the following vs. (10b) does refer to the physical object.

In c my тАЬknows his way aroundтАЭ is a literal calque of p├бri v├йd─Б into an English idiom (cf. almost identical passage I.31.5). (A more chaste rendering would have been тАЬthoroughly knows.тАЭ) In both passages we might have expected univerbation of the preverb and verb with loss of accent on p├бri in the rel. cl.; I have no explanation for why this did not happen, save for the possibility that p├бri does not function as a conventional preverb but as an adverb or postposition and also given the fact that such univerbation is not generally obligatory.

Geldner and Renou take c with d rather than ab; this is certainly possible and there are no implications either way.

Griffith

Agni, the mortal who hath toiled and worshipped, brought thee oblations with his kindled fuel,
And well knows sacrifice with adoration, gains every joy with thee to guard and help him.

Geldner

Der Sterbliche, o Agni, hat geopfert und den Dienst versehen, der mit Brennholz deinen Opferanteil ausgerichtet hat. Wer die Opferung unter Verbeugungen gr├╝ndlich versteht, der empf├дngt mit deiner Hilfe alles Gute.

Grassmann

Der Mensch, o Agni, hat gewirkt, geopfert, der dir mit Brennholz Opfergabe weihte; Wer recht versteht den Opferguss in Ehrfurcht, empf├дngt durch dich die sch├╢nsten G├╝ter alle.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo you, mighty Agni, we offer exceeding adoration with prostrations, with fuel, with oblations; (we glorify you) on the altar, son of strength, with hymns and with prayers; may we be successful in our efforts (to gain) you auspicious favour.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To you right here, the great one, great honor would we do, with acts of homage, o Agni, with kindling wood, and with oblations,
with the altar, o son of strength, with hymns, with solemn words. May we take our place in your auspicious benevolence.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The doubling of the 2nd sg. enclitic te by init. asma├н, the here-and-now demonstrative, is somewhat unusual, though in the same general vein as t├бс╣Г tv─Б (2c, 6c, 7a).

Geldner and Renou (see also Klein I.329, Oberlies II.133) take v├йd─л as a loc., but in this passage, embedded in a long series of instrumentals, there seems no reason not to interpr. it as the instr. it appears to be. See AiG III.155, where Wack identifies it as an instr. here. The very similar passage VI.13.4 y├бs te s┼лno sahaso g─лrbh├нr uktha├нс╕е тАж vedy─Б╠Бnaс╣н (that is, probably to be emended to *v├йdy─Б╠Бnaс╣н and analyzed *v├йdy─Б тАж), supports the instr. interpr. – which is argued for for both passages by Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions ad VI.1.10) and Oldenberg (Noten ad VI.13.4).

Renou (see also Klein I.52, 71) take bh─Бs─Б╠Б, ┼Ыr├бvobhi┼Ы ca as a conjoined NP, with Renou putting immediately following ┼Ыravasy├ас╕е into a separate syntagm (Klein doesnтАЩt treat anything but the two nouns). Although ca does generally conjoin nominals, both the p─Бda break between the instrumentals and the etymological figure ┼Ыr├бvobhiс╕е тАж ┼Ыravasy├ас╕е suggest that the two instr. belong with different parts of the clause.

English translation:

тАЬDo you, Agni, who have spread heaven and earth with light, who are the preserver (of man), and (who are) to be glorified with praises, shine brightly upon us with abundant food, and with substantial riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You who stretch through the two world-halves with your light and who through (words of) fame deserve to be famed as surpassing,
with lofty substantial prizes for us, with rich ones, Agni, radiate out more widely.

Griffith

Thou who hast covered heaven and earth with splendour and with thy glories, glorious and triumphant.
Continue thou to shine on us, O Agni, with strength abundant, rich, and long enduring.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPossessor of wealth, bestow upon us at all times opulence conjoined with dependants, and (grant) abundance of cattle to our sons and grandsons; may therefore be to us abundant food, satisfying our wishes, and free from blame; and may there be auspicious and reputable (means of subsistence).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O good one, manfully establish for us forever and for our progeny and posterity abundance of livestock.
Let there be for us many lofty refreshments that keep evil at a distance and auspicious things bringing good fame.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take nс╣Ыv├бt as an adverb, since this neut. is almost always so used. Geldner and Renou instead take it as a full adj. тАШconsisting of men, accompanied by menтАЩ modifying a gapped noun (Besitz, la richesse) and implicitly parallel to bh┼л╠Бri тАж pa┼Ыv├бс╕е тАЬabundance of livestock.тАЭ I am not convinced, and curiously the passage Geldner cites in his n. 10a as support for the interpr. contains a nс╣Ыv├бt that must be adverbial. Still, I do have to admit that a few such expressions do exist outside of the neut. sg.: I.92.7 nrv├бta ╠е с╕е тАж v─Б╠Бj─Бn, IX.93.5 ray├нm … nrv├бntam ╠е .

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. play on the two words pur├║- тАШmanyтАЩ and v├бsu- тАШgoodтАЩ in this final explosion of begging for a suitable return from the god.

Vouchsafe us ever, as man needs, O Vasu, abundant wealth of kine for son and offspring.
Food noble, plenteous, far from sin and evil, he with us, and fair fame to make us happy.

Verleih uns, du Guter, immerdar Besitz von Mannen, viel Vieh f├╝r den leiblichen Samen, viele gro├Яe Speisegen├╝sse, die das ├Ьbel fern halten. Guter Ruf soll uns zuteil werden!

English translation:

тАЬRoyal Agni, may I obtain from you your many and various treasures whereby to be enriched; for, Agni, who are the desired of multitudes, infinite are the riches (aggregated) in you, fit, monarch, for your worshipper.тАЭ

Many goods many-fold in their goodness might I attain of you through seeking you, o King Agni.
For many are the goods in you, o Agni of many favors, for the one who does (you) honor, since you are king. с│У

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН ! рддреЗ рдпрд╛ рд╡рд╕реБрддрд╛ рддрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд┐ рдкреБрд░реВрдгрд┐ рдкреБрд░реБрдзрд╛ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдпрд╛ рд╕рд╣рд╛рд╜рд╣рдорд╢реНрдпрд╛рдореНред рд╣реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗ ! рд╣рд┐ рддреНрд╡реЗ рдкреБрд░реВрдгрд┐ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рд░рд╛рдЬрдирд┐ рддреНрд╡реЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдзрддреЗ рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдВ рдЬрд╛рдпрддреЗ рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдорд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рднрд╡ реерезрейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдереЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╡рддреНрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдкреБрд░реВрдгрд┐) рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН (рдкреБрд░реБрдзрд╛) рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реИрд░реНрдзрд╛рд░рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рддреНрд╡рд╛рдпрд╛) рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рд╕рд╣ (рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐) рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ (рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдпрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди (рд╡рд╕реБрддрд╛) рд╡рд╕реВрдирд╛рдВ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рднрд╛рд╡рдГ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдЕрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдореН (рдкреБрд░реВрдгрд┐) рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐ (рд╣рд┐) рдЦрд▓реБ (рддреНрд╡реЗ) рддреНрд╡рдпрд┐ (рдкреБрд░реБрд╡рд╛рд░) рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд░рдгреАрдп (рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐) (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдпрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди (рд╡рд╕реБ) рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдореН (рд╡рд┐рдзрддреЗ) рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреЗ (рд░рд╛рдЬрдирд┐) (рддреНрд╡реЗ) рддреНрд╡рдпрд┐ реерезрейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдд рдПрд╡ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рди рдЙрддреНрддрдорд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпреЗ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╡рддреНрдкрдХреНрд╖рдкрд╛рддрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдп рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╡рддреНрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛ рдПрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬреЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рднрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдиреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ реерезрейрее рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рд╕рд╡рд┐рддреГрдорд░реБрджрдЧреНрдиреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдорддреНрдкрд░рдорд╣рдВрд╕рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реНрд░рд╛рдЬрдХрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрд╡рд┐рд░рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрджрд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреАрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирд╛рдВ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпреЗрдг рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреАрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрд╛рд╜рд╜рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рднрд╛рд╖рд╛рд╡рд┐рднреВрд╖рд┐рдд рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрджрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдерд╛рд╖реНрдЯрдХреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЛрд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрдГ рд╖рдЯреНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рднреЗрджрднрд╛рд╡ рди рдХрд░рддрд╛ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдЪреЗ рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддреЗрдЪ рд░рд╛рдЬреЗ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд. рдЬреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╡ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЪреЗ рднрдХреНрдд рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд рддреЗрдЪ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрди рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд. рее резрей рее
